🧑 User

Please explain the enemy selection algorithm for each wave.

🤖 Assistant

The enemy selection algorithm in this project uses a "Budget-based Weighted Random Selection" approach.

The main mechanism consists of the following 3 steps.

1. Determining the Budget

Each time a wave starts, the total cost (budget) available for that wave is calculated.

  • Formula: InitialWaveBudget + (WaveCount - 1) * BudgetIncreasePerWave
  • Enemies are selected one at a time until this budget is exhausted (or until even the cheapest enemy can no longer be afforded).
  • Each enemy has a cost called Level (e.g., a Slime costs 2), which is deducted from the budget each time one is selected.

2. Dynamic Weighted Random Selection

This is the most distinctive part of the algorithm — a mechanism that "dynamically changes which enemy types are more likely to appear based on game progression."

  • Weight formula: $\text{Weight} = \text{EnemyLevel}^\text{power}$
  • Exponent (power): $-1.0 + (\text{WaveCount} / 10.0)$

As the power value changes with the wave count, the selection tendency shifts:

  • Early game (Waves 1–9): power becomes negative (e.g., -0.9).
    • Enemies with lower levels get higher weights, making weak enemies like Slimes appear in large numbers.
  • Mid game (around Wave 10): power approaches 0.
    • All enemies are selected with roughly equal probability.
  • Late game (Wave 11 onward): power becomes positive.
    • Enemies with higher levels get exponentially larger weights, causing powerful enemies to be selected preferentially.

3. Selection Limits

  • Minimum cost: Selection ends when the budget drops below 2.
  • Spawn count limit: In the simulator, a maximum of 5 enemies; in the actual game, limited by the number of spawn points (EnemySpawnPoints).

Summary

This algorithm automatically generates a natural difficulty curve — "waves of weak enemies early on, varied compositions in the mid game, and powerful elite enemies in the late game" — without the need to manually create lists.

🧑 User

Please make the "/10.0" part in the power calculation adjustable via GameBalanceData.

🤖 Assistant

I extracted the coefficient 10.0 used when calculating enemy selection weights as WaveWeightShiftFactor, making it adjustable from GameBalanceData.

Changes Made

  1. GameBalanceData.cs: Added the new WaveWeightShiftFactor (default value: 10.0).
  2. CombatManager.cs: Updated the actual enemy spawn logic to reference balanceData.WaveWeightShiftFactor instead of the hardcoded 10.0f.
  3. GameBalanceSimulationWindow.cs: Updated the simulator's calculation logic in the same way, so that changes to this coefficient are immediately reflected in the predicted results.
  4. GameBalanceDataEditor.cs: Configured the field to appear in the Inspector with a descriptive label.

Tuning Tips

  • Lower value (e.g., 5.0): Enemies become stronger more quickly. High-level enemies start appearing earlier.
  • Higher value (e.g., 20.0): The enemy composition shifts more gradually. Low-level enemies remain in the mix for longer.

This allows you to freely adjust the transition speed of difficulty "quality" (which types of enemies are more likely to appear) directly from the Inspector.

🧑 User

Is this value also reflected in the Example Party Composition of the Balance Simulator?

🤖 Assistant

Yes, it is correctly reflected in Example Party Composition as well.

With the earlier fix (changes to GameBalanceSimulationWindow.cs), the calculation logic inside the simulator has also been rewritten to reference balanceData.WaveWeightShiftFactor.

// GameBalanceSimulationWindow.cs 内の修正箇所
float power = -1.0f + (float)previewWave / balanceData.WaveWeightShiftFactor;

How Reflection Works

  1. When the slider is operated: Moving the Target Wave slider recalculates the "appearance weights" using the WaveWeightShiftFactor value at that point in time.
  2. When data is changed: Rewriting the WaveWeightShiftFactor value in the Inspector sends a notification to the simulator window, and the contents displayed in Example Party Composition are updated immediately.

For example, if you set WaveWeightShiftFactor to an extremely small value (e.g., 2.0), you should be able to confirm in the window that the enemy composition displayed becomes skewed toward stronger ones (higher-cost enemies) even for the same wave count.

🧑 User

When I tested on a mobile browser (touchscreen), I was unable to operate the block Shutter. Does it not support touch input? Please investigate and provide only your answer.

🤖 Assistant

The current implementation does not support touch input.

As a result of investigation, it was found that the input handling in GridManager.cs (the Update method) references only Mouse.current (mouse input) from the new Input System.

Technical Cause

  1. Mouse-only code: The code directly uses Mouse.current.leftButton.wasPressedThisFrame and Mouse.current.position.ReadValue(), which do not accept input from anything other than a physical mouse (or an environment where mouse emulation is enabled).
  2. Lack of touch handling: Touchscreen.current (touchscreen input) and the Pointer class (Pointer.current), which can abstractly handle both mouse and touch input, are not being used.

Solution (Approach)

To resolve this issue, the references to Mouse.current need to be rewritten to use Pointer.current, or the code needs to be modified to monitor both mouse and touch input. This will allow block operations (clicking/tapping) to work on mobile browser touchscreens as well.
